du">Share</p></div></button></div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div><p id="8988" class="pw-post-body-paragraph nk nl gv bf b ht nm nn no hw np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od oe go bk of"><span class="l og oh oi bo oj ok ol om on fj">A</span>fter a customer asked me yesterday whether I already knew the Kapeka backdoor and whether it could be blocked using the latest Sysmon configuration, I’ve analyzed the backdoor yesterday and wrote SIEM customized detection rules (example for threat hunting see below).</p><blockquote class="oo op oq"><p id="8325" class="nk nl or bf b ht nm nn no hw np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od oe go bk">T<!-- -->he malware, which we are calling “Kapeka”, is a flexible backdoor with all the necessary functionalities to serve as an early-stage toolkit for its operators, and also to provide long-term access to the victim estate. The malware’s victimology, infrequent sightings, and level of stealth and sophistication indicate APT-level activity. <a class="af ii" href="https://labs.withsecure.com/publications/kapeka" rel="noopener ugc nofollow" target="_blank">W/Labs</a></p></blockquote><p id="24a6" class="pw-post-body-paragraph nk nl gv bf b ht nm nn no hw np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od oe go bk">Less than 24 hours later, the Ukrainian CERT published its latest alert about an attempt to disrupt critical infrastructure. Here again the attacker is <strong class="bf os">APT44</strong> and this time it is the backdoor <strong class="bf os">QUEUESEED</strong>, which is identical to KAPEKA used in June 2022 in Ukraine (same hash, almost same behavior). Therefore, I decided to translate the current UA-CERT article and enrich it with technical information.</p><p id="2b76" class="pw-post-body-paragraph nk nl gv bf b ht nm nn no hw np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od oe go bk">Mandiant <a class="af ii" href="https://cloud.google.com/blog/topics/threat-intelligence/apt44-unearthing-sandworm" rel="noopener ugc nofollow" target="_blank">describes SIX Phases of APT44 </a>disruptive operations during the 2022 war in Ukraine and now the 7th phase could be potentially the non-kinetic attempt to disrupt again with the same backdoors like <strong class="bf os">KAPEKA</strong> from June 2022 which was used with <strong class="bf os">SDELETE</strong>. Exact the same hash is now in this article for <strong class="bf os">UAC-0133</strong> the <strong class="bf os">QUEUESEED</strong> backdoor with the same technical behavior including the SDELETE.</p><figure class="ow ox oy oz pa pb ot ou paragraph-image"><div role="button" tabindex="0" class="pc pd fj pe bh pf"><div class="ot ou ov"><picture><source alt="" class="bh mr pg c" width="700" height="255" loading="lazy" role="presentation"/></picture></div></div><figcaption class="ph ff pi ot ou pj pk bf b bg z du">WithSecure Research Kapeka with a in-depth technical analysis of the backdoor</figcaption></figure><h1 id="3ebe" class="pm pn gv bf po pp pq hv pr ps pt hy pu pv pw px py pz qa qb qc qd qe qf qg qh bk">Some Threat Hunting opportunities for both backdoors</h1><p id="114c" class="pw-post-body-paragraph nk nl gv bf b ht qi nn no hw qj nq nr ns qk nu nv nw ql ny nz oa qm oc od oe go bk">I’ve found the example for <strong class="bf os">KAPEKA</strong>/<strong class="bf os">QUEUESEED </strong>in AnyRun, Virus Total and some more Sandboxes and tested it additionally. A more technical view in the Dr.WEB vxCube Sandbox shows the process creation and execution of the dropped <strong class="bf os">.wll</strong> file that is randomly changing the name while the command stays the same. The same I’ve found out for the batch file that is created to delete the artifact again, means the initial file <strong class="bf os">crdss.exe</strong> which seems not to change the name and is an invariant behavior for the backdoor. Like mentioned before the same executable is used by Sandworm since at least June 2022 in the Ukrainian conflict. The self-deletion batch file which is deleting crdss.exe has a different name each time it is created. It is hidden in the <strong class="bf os">AppData </strong>or <strong class="bf os">Tmp</strong> folder (in my own test).</p><p id="2b98" class="pw-post-body-paragraph nk nl gv bf b ht nm nn no hw np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od oe go bk"><strong class="bf os">Example KAPEKA for the batch file</strong></p><p id="cf28" class="pw-post-body-paragraph nk nl gv bf b ht nm nn no hw np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od oe go bk"><em class="or">C:\Windows\system32\cmd.exe /c “C:\Users\admin\AppData\qehe.bat”</em></p><p id="e762" class="pw-post-body-paragraph nk nl gv bf b ht nm nn no hw np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od oe go bk"><strong class="bf os">Example QUEESEED in the UA-CERT article</strong></p><p id="4b5a" class="pw-post-body-paragraph nk nl gv bf b ht nm nn no hw np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od oe go bk"><em class="or">%COMSPEC% /c %APPDATA%\pizi.bat</em></p><p id="8651" class="pw-post-body-paragraph nk nl gv bf b ht nm nn no hw np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od oe go bk">The persistence of both backdoors is ensured by a dropper that creates a corresponding scheduled task or entry in the “Run” branch of the Windows registry.</p><p id="af73" class="pw-post-body-paragraph nk nl gv bf b ht nm nn no hw np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od oe go bk"><strong class="bf os">Here are additionally the registry entries for the backdoor for SENS API</strong> (<strong class="bf os">KAPEKA example </strong><a class="af ii" href="https://app.any.run/tasks/020b1371-103d-47c2-8731-6d7bcf9b3bf1/" rel="noopener ugc nofollow" target="_blank"><strong class="bf os">AnyRun</strong></a>):</p><p id="5b3c" class="pw-post-body-paragraph nk nl gv bf b ht nm nn no hw np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od oe go bk"><em class="or">C:\WINDOWS\system32\cmd.exe” /c REG ADD</em></p><p id="5f1a" class="pw-post-body-paragraph nk nl gv bf b ht nm nn no hw np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od oe go bk"><em class="or">HKCU\SOFTWARE\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Run /v “Sens Api” /t REG_SZ /d “C:\WINDOWS\system32\rundll32.exe \”C:\Users\admin\AppData\Local\Microsoft\cujuni.wll\”, #1&quot; /f</em></p><p id="3ba2" class="pw-post-body-paragraph nk nl gv bf b ht nm nn no hw np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od oe go bk"><em class="or">REG ADD HKCU\SOFTWARE\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Run /v “Sens Api” /t REG_SZ /d “C:\WINDOWS\system32\rundll32.exe \”C:\Users\admin\AppData\Local\Microsoft\cujuni.wll\”, #1&quot; /f</em></p><p id="c193" class="pw-post-body-paragraph nk nl gv bf b ht nm nn no hw np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od oe go bk">A<strong class="bf os">nother example of KAPEKA for T1547 Registry Run Keys /Startup Folder persistence</strong>:</p><p id="2f3a" class="pw-post-body-paragraph nk nl gv bf b ht nm nn no hw np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od oe go bk"><em class="or">C:\Windows\system32\rundll32.exe “C:\Users\admin\AppData\Local\Microsoft\jagyg.wll”, #1</em></p><p id="32d3" class="pw-post-body-paragraph nk nl gv bf b ht nm nn no hw np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od oe go bk"><strong class="bf os">And the latest Ukrainian CERT article scheduled task SENS API for QUEUESEED:</strong></p><p id="9bfa" class="pw-post-body-paragraph nk nl gv bf b ht nm nn no hw np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od oe go bk"><em class="or">%COMSPEC% /c schtasks /create /sc ONSTART /tn “Sens Api” /f /np /tr %WINDIR%\system32\rundll32.exe %PROGRAMDATA%\Microsoft\lunose.wll, #1</em></p><p id="f63b" class="pw-post-body-paragraph nk nl gv bf b ht nm nn no hw np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od oe go bk"><strong class="bf os">Another artifact in the Ukrainian CERT article for the persistence:</strong></p><p id="c8ca" class="pw-post-body-paragraph nk nl gv bf b ht nm nn no hw np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od oe go bk"><em class="or">C:\Windows\system32\rundll32.exe “%PROGRAMDATA%\Microsoft\hasuti.wll”, #1</em></p><p id="f857" class="pw-post-body-paragraph nk nl gv bf b ht nm nn no hw np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od oe go bk">Both have the <strong class="bf os"><em class="or">/c schtasks /create /sc ONSTART /tn “Sens Api” /f /np /tr with</em></strong><em class="or"> </em>and<em class="or"> </em><strong class="bf os"><em class="or">.wll </em></strong>for robust detection<strong class="bf os"><em class="or">. </em></strong>The paths for the persistence and the batch file can differ within the backdoors, but the commands, dropper, self-deletion etc. are the same.</p><p id="a8ac" class="pw-post-body-paragraph nk nl gv bf b ht nm nn no hw np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od oe go bk of"><span class="l og oh oi bo oj ok ol om on fj">T</span>he following content is the translation of the latest UA-CERT article about Sandworm and the latest assumption that the cyberattacks are used as an attempt to disrupt the critical infrastructure while missile strikes on infrastructure facilities in Ukraine enhance the destructive effect.</p><p id="01e9" class="pw-post-body-paragraph nk nl gv bf b ht nm nn no hw np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od oe go bk"><strong class="bf os">General Information</strong></p><p id="56f5" class="pw-post-body-paragraph nk nl gv bf b ht nm nn no hw np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od oe go bk">In March 2024, the Government Computer Emergency Response Team of Ukraine (CERT-UA) uncovered a malicious plan of the Sandworm group aimed at disrupting the sustainable functioning of information and communication systems (ICS) of about twenty enterprises in the field of energy, water and heat supply (OKI) in ten regions of Ukraine.</p><p id="b069" class="pw-post-body-paragraph nk nl gv bf b ht nm nn no hw np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od oe go bk">In addition to the <strong class="bf os">QUEUESEED</strong> backdoor (<strong class="bf os">KNUCKLETOUCH, ICYWELL</strong>, <strong class="bf os">wrongsens, kapeka</strong>) known since 2022, a new toolkit of attackers was detected, namely, malware <strong class="bf os">LOADGRIP</strong> and <strong class="bf os">BIASBOAT</strong> (Linux variant of QUEUESEED), which were installed on computers (Linux OS), designed to automate process control processes (APCS) using specialized software of domestic production. It should be noted that BIASBOAT was presented in the form of a file encrypted for a specific server, for which the attackers used the pre-obtained value “machine-id”.</p><p id="eb8a" class="pw-post-body-paragraph nk nl gv bf b ht nm nn no hw np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od oe go bk">CERT-UA specialists confirmed the facts of compromise of at least three “supply chains”, in connection with which the circumstances of the initial unauthorized access either correlate with the installation of SDRs, which contained software bookmarks and vulnerabilities, or are caused by the regular technical ability of the supplier’s employees to access the ICS of organizations for maintenance and technical support.</p><p id="b075" class="pw-post-body-paragraph nk nl gv bf b ht nm nn no hw np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od oe go bk">Taking into account the functioning of computers with SDRs within the ICS OKI, the attackers used them for horizontal movement and the development of a cyberattack against corporate networks of enterprises. For example, on such computers, a pre-created <strong class="bf os">PHP webshell</strong> <strong class="bf os">WEEVELY</strong> and a <strong class="bf os">PHP tunnel REGEORG</strong> were found in the catalogs with SDRs. <strong class="bf os">NEO</strong> or <strong class="bf os">PIVOTNACCI</strong>.</p><p id="ae36" class="pw-post-body-paragraph nk nl gv bf b ht nm nn no hw np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od oe go bk of"><span class="l og oh oi bo oj ok ol om on fj">In</span> the period from 07.03.2024 to 15.03.2024, CERT-UA specialists took measures to inform all identified enterprises and investigate and counter cyber threats in the relevant ICS, within the framework of which the circumstances of the initial compromise were established, malware was seized and analyzed, a chronology of incident events was built, assistance in setting up server and active network equipment, and protection technology was installed (at some <strong class="bf os">LOADGRIP/BIASBOAT</strong> enterprises there was created in 2023).</p><p id="84c9" class="pw-post-body-paragraph nk nl gv bf b ht nm nn no hw np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od oe go bk">It should be emphasized that the attackers used <strong class="bf os">QUEUESEED </strong>and GOSSIPFLOW malware on Windows computers, which have been monitored since 2022 in the context of destructive cyberattacks by the UAC-0133 group on <strong class="bf os">water supply facilities</strong>, in particular, using <strong class="bf os">SDELETE</strong>. Thus, with a high level of confidence, <strong class="bf os">UAC-0133 is a subcluster of UAC-0002 (Sandworm/APT44).</strong></p><p id="7698" class="pw-post-body-paragraph nk nl gv bf b ht nm nn no hw np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od oe go bk">It should be noted that the following factors contributed to the implementation of cyberattacks:</p><ul class=""><li id="bd6b" class="nk nl gv bf b ht nm nn no hw np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od oe qn qo qp bk">incorrect segmentation (lack of isolation) of servers with <strong class="bf os">SDR</strong>s of suppliers used as an element of the process control system, in the context of both <strong class="bf os">restriction of access to/to the Internet and ICS</strong> of the organizations within which they operate</li><li id="eb86" class="nk nl gv bf b ht qq nn no hw qr nq nr ns qs nu nv nw qt ny nz oa qu oc od oe qn qo qp bk"><strong class="bf os">negligent attitude of suppliers to the security of software</strong> provided to consumers; in particular, a superficial analysis of the source code will reveal <strong class="bf os">trivial vulnerabilities that allow</strong> <strong class="bf os">remote code execution (RCE)</strong>.</li></ul><h2 id="8968" class="qv pn gv bf po qw qx dy pr qy qz ea pu ns ra rb rc nw rd re rf oa rg rh ri rj bk">Enhance the effect of missile strikes</h2><p id="90fa" class="pw-post-body-paragraph nk nl gv bf b ht qi nn no hw qj nq nr ns qk nu nv nw ql ny nz oa qm oc od oe go bk">CERT-UA assumes that unauthorized access to ICS for a significant number of heat, water and energy supply facilities should have been used to enhance the effect of missile strikes on infrastructure facilities in Ukraine in the spring of 2024.</p><p id="fa77" class="pw-post-body-paragraph nk nl gv bf b ht nm nn no hw np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od oe go bk">QUEUESEED is a malicious program developed using the <strong class="bf os">C++</strong> programming language. Receives basic information about the computer (OS, language, user name), executes commands received from the control server and sends the result. Functions: read/write files, execute commands (as a standalone process, or via <strong class="bf os">%COMSPEC%/c</strong>), <strong class="bf os">update configuration, self-delete</strong>. <strong class="bf os">HTTPS</strong> is used to interact with the management server. The data is transmitted in <strong class="bf os">JSON</strong> format and encrypted using <strong class="bf os">RSA+AES</strong>. The backdoor configuration file, which in particular contains the URL of the management server, is encrypted using AES (the key is statically set in the program). Implemented queue of raw incoming commands/results — stored in the Windows registry in AES-encrypted form (the value %MACHINEGUID is used as the key). <strong class="bf os">The persistence of the backdoor is ensured by a dropper that creates a corresponding scheduled task or entry in the “Run” branch of the Windows registry.</strong></p><p id="0332" class="pw-post-body-paragraph nk nl gv bf b ht nm nn no hw np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od oe go bk"><strong class="bf os">BIASBOAT</strong>, a malicious program <strong class="bf os">(ELF)</strong> developed using the C programming language, is a <strong class="bf os">Linux variant of QUEUESEED</strong>. Starting on the computer is carried out using the <strong class="bf os">LOADGRIP</strong> injector.</p><p id="ffa1" class="pw-post-body-paragraph nk nl gv bf b ht nm nn no hw np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od oe go bk"><strong class="bf os">LOADGRIP</strong> is a malicious program <strong class="bf os">(ELF) </strong>developed using the C programming language. The payload is usually presented in encrypted form (AES128-CBC), and the key for its decryption is formed on the basis of the constants statically specified in the code and the value of the “machine-id” of the computer.</p><p id="7c31" class="pw-post-body-paragraph nk nl gv bf b ht nm nn no hw np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od oe go bk"><strong class="bf os">GOSSIPFLOW</strong> is a malicious program developed using the <strong class="bf os">Go programming language</strong>. Provides tunneling (uses the Yamux multiplexer library) and performs the functionality of a <strong class="bf os">SOCKS5 proxy</strong>.</p><p id="5b48" class="pw-post-body-paragraph nk nl gv bf b ht nm nn no hw np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od oe go bk">In addition to the above-mentioned software tools for implementing cyber threats, the group also used, but not exclusively:</p><ul class=""><li id="c31a" class="nk nl gv bf b ht nm nn no hw np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od oe qn qo qp bk"><strong class="bf os">CHISEL</strong></li><li id="8aa3" class="nk nl gv bf b ht qq nn no hw qr nq nr ns qs nu nv nw qt ny nz oa qu oc od oe qn qo qp bk"><strong class="bf os">LIBPROCESSHIDER</strong></li><li id="30ce" class="nk nl gv bf b ht qq nn no hw qr nq nr ns qs nu nv nw qt ny nz oa qu oc od oe qn qo qp bk"><strong class="bf os">JUICYPOTATONG</strong></li><li id="fce0" class="nk nl gv bf b ht qq nn no hw qr nq nr ns qs nu nv nw qt ny nz oa qu oc od oe qn qo qp bk"><strong class="bf os">ROTTENPOTATONG</strong></li></ul><p id="ab9b" class="pw-post-body-paragraph nk nl gv bf b ht nm nn no hw np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od oe go bk"><strong
